API gravity is measured by a hydrometer instrument having a scale graduated in degrees API.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Backhaul</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - A deviation to move cargo on the return leg of a voyage for the purpose of minimizing ballast mileage and thereby reducing transportation cost. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Bare Boat Charter </span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">- A Charter in which the bare ship is chartered without crew; the charterer, for a stipulated sum taking over the vessel with a minimum of restrictions usually for 10 or more years. See Demise Charter. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Barrel</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - The standard unit of liquid volume in the petroleum industry. It is equal to 42 U.S. gallons. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Canceling Date</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - A stated date after which, if a vessel is not ready to load, the intending charterers have the option of canceling the charter. The passing of the canceling date leaves the owner\u2019s obligation unimpaired unless the charterer releases him. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Bareboat Charter</span></b><span style=\"font-size: />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Contract of Affreightment (COA)</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - A service contract under which a ship owner agrees to transport a specified quantity of fuel products or specialty products, at a specified rate per ton between designated loading and discharge ports. This type contract differs from a spot or consecutive voyage charter in that no particular vessel is specified. (Rates are usually discounted below other forms of contracts.) <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Spot (Voyage) Charter</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - A charter for a particular vessel to move a single cargo between specified loading port(s) and discharge port(s) in the immediate future. Contract rate (spot rate) covers total operating expenses such as port charges, bunkering, crew expenses, insurance, repairs, and canal tolls. The charterer will generally pay all cargo-related costs.<span style=\"color: black; letter-spacing: .05pt;\"> T</span><span style=\"color: black; letter-spacing: .1pt;\">h</span><span style=\"color: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; tab-stops: 138.0pt; text-autospace: none;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Time Charter (T/C)</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - A charter for varying periods of time, usually between two and ten years, under which the owner hires out the vessel to the shipper fully manned, provisioned, stored and insured. The charterer is usually responsible for bunkers, port charges, canal tolls and any crew overtime connected with the cargo. />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Classification of Petroleum</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - Classes \"A-C\" of petroleum are considered flammable and have a flash point of 80\u00b0 F or below. Examples of these classes range from very light napthas (Class A) to most crude oils (Class C). Class D cargoes such as kerosene and heavy crudes are considered combustible and have a flash point above 80\u00b0 F but below 150\u00b0 F. Class E cargoes are the heavier fuel oils and lubricating oils and have a flash point above 150\u00b0 F. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; tab-stops: 138.0pt; text-autospace: none;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: the detention of the vessel under charter at the expiration of laytime allowed. <span style=\"color: black;\">C<span style=\"letter-spacing: .1pt;\">o</span>mp<span style=\"letter-spacing: 150%;\">Deviation</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - A departure from a voyage pattern on either the forward or return leg of a voyage. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Dirty Service</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - Tanker transportation of crudes and residual fuels. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Dispatch</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - The function of issuing voyage instructions or sailing orders to vessels. Also an agreed amount to be charged by terminals for prompt vessel turn around. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Displacement Tonnage</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - Expressed in tons it is the weight the water displaced by the vessel which in turn is the weight of the vessel at that time. The vessel\u2019s light displacement is the weight of the vessel only and the vessel\u2019s loaded displacement is the weight of the vessel and all cargo, stores, fuel, water, etc. on board. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Disponent Owner</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - Charterer who has sublet the vessel and is acting as the owner per the terms of the contract. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Ensign</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - The flag carried by a ship as insignia of her nationality. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Filling Density</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - The ratio of the weight of liquid in a tank to the weight of distilled water at 60\u00b0 F. the tank will hold. It is expressed as a percent. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Flame Screen</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> (or Arrester) - A device comprised of a fine wire gauze that is fitted into the discharge end of a vent line. It prevents the passage of flame, but will allow vapor to pass through. Flame screens are also fitted to removable ullage plugs used to cover ullage holes on cargo tank tops. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Force Majeure</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - Clause permitting contract to be broken in the event of uncontrollable events, e.g. war, strike government action, which preclude its fulfillment. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Free Discharge (FD)</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - The charterer is responsible for the cost of unloading the cargo. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Free In And Out (FIO)</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - The charterer is responsible for both the costs of loading and unloading the cargo. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Free on Board (FOB)</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - The charterer is responsible for the cost of loading the cargo. style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Gas Free Certificate</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - A certificate issued by a chemist after sampling the air in a tanker's cargo tanks after the cargo has been pumped out. It is endorsed with one of the following notations: (1) Safe for men, (2) Not safe for fire, (3) Safe for men and fire, (4) Not safe. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">General Average</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - A general contribution of money paid by all parties concerned in a marine adventure in direct proportion to their several interests when a voluntary or deliberate sacrifice has been made of one or more of the party\u2019s goods in time of peril with a view to saving the remainder of the property. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Gross Tonnage</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - The internal capacity of a vessel measured in units of 100 cubic feet.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Guarantee Items</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - Repair of guarantee items that develop during the first year of service of a new vessel and are usually corrected by the builder under a guarantee. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">In Class</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> \u2013 A vessel currently meeting all the requirements of its Classification Society is \"in-class\". <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"color: black; font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.1pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"color: black; font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.1pt; line-height: 150%;\">In</span></b><b><span style=\"color: black; -.15pt;\">e</span></span><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Inert Gas (IG)</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - A gas used by marine tank vessels to displace air in cargo tanks to reduce oxygen content to 8 percent or less by volume and thus reduce possibility of fire or explosion. The inert gas used is usually nitrogen, carbon dioxide or a mixture of gases such as flue gas.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Inert Gas System (IGS)</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - A mechanical method of introducing inert gas into a vessel\u2019s tanks. An inert gas is one which has little or no ability to react with other gases, or to heat. Examples of inert gases are nitrogen and CO2. Shipboard inert gas systems utilize CO2, either from flue gas sources or from inert gas generators. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Inerting</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - A procedure used to reduce the oxygen content of a vessel\u2019s cargo spaces to 8 percent or less by volume by introducing an \"inert\" gas blanket such as nitrogen or carbon dioxide or a mixture of gases such as flue gas.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span 150%;\">Innage</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - The amount of space within a tank that is occupied by oil. Innages are sometimes called soundings or body gauges. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Independent Inspector (Cargo Surveyor)</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - A person or organization of persons acting independently, but on behalf of, one or more parties involved in the transfer, storage, inventory or analysis of a commodity for purposes of determining the quantity, and/or quality of a commodity. They may also be assigned to the calibration of various measurement instruments and/or storage tanks ashore or on vessels.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Intake Certificate</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - A document issued by the shipper indicating the amount of cargo loaded aboard the vessel as calculated from the shore tank gauges. The charterer is not obliged to start loading before the commencement of lay days. The charterer may cancel the charter if the ship does not tender prior to the expiration of lay days. The distinction between a lighter and a barge is more in the manner of use than in equipment. The term \"lighter\" refers to a short haul, generally in connection with loading and unloading operations of vessels in harbor while the term \"barge\" is more often used when the cargo is being carried to its destination or over a long distance. <b>2)</b> To load or discharge cargo to or from another vessel. </span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -.25pt;\">o</span>f<span style=\"letter-spacing: -.1pt;\"> </span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -.15pt;\">L</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -.15pt;\">a</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: .25pt;\">n</span>d<span style=\"letter-spacing: -.05pt;\"> </span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -.15pt;\">t</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: .25pt;\">h</span>e<span style=\"letter-spacing: -.2pt;\"> </span>q<span style=\"letter-spacing: -.25pt;\">u</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -.15pt;\">a</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: .25pt;\">n</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -.15pt;\">t</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: .1pt;\">it</span>y<span style=\"letter-spacing: -.2pt;\"> </span><span style=\"letter-spacing: </span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -.25pt;\">o</span>n<span style=\"letter-spacing: .15pt;\"> </span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -.15pt;\">t</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: mso-font-width: 101%;\">e</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: .25pt;\">r</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -.15pt; mso-font-width: 101%;\">t</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: .1pt; mso-font-width: 101%;\">c</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: .1pt; mso-font-width: 101%;\">at</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -.15pt; mso-font-width: 101%;\">e</span>.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Procedure</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">: <b>Load on top</b> is the shipboard procedure of collecting and settling water and oil mixtures, resulting from ballasting and tank cleaning operations (usually in a special slop tank or tanks), and subsequently loading cargo on top of and pumping the mixture ashore at the discharge port. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Practice</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">: Load on top is the act of commingling on-board quantity with cargo being loaded. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Loaded Passage</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - The passage during which the tanker is carrying cargo. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Long Ton</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - A unit of weight = 2,240 pounds or 1,106 kilos. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Marine Custody Transfer (MCT)</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - A custody transfer activity involving a marine tank vessel(s). Loading, discharging or lightering a ship or barge is a marine custody transfer.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Marine Surveyor</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - A duly qualified person who examines ships to ascertain their condition, on behalf of owners, underwriters, etc. Also called \"ship surveyor\" or simply \"surveyor\". <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Maritime Law</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - That system of jurisprudence that prevails in courts having jurisdiction of marine causes. Also called marine or admiralty law. It is a branch of both international and commercial law. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Metric Ton</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> \u2013 A unit of weight 2,204.6 pounds (1,000 kilograms). <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Midship Draft</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - The draft read at the midship markings. This draft can, and often does, differ from the Mean Draft due to hogging or sagging. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Net Registered Tonnage</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - The internal capacity of a vessel measured in units of 100 cubic feet less the space occupied by boilers, engines, shaft alleys, chain lockers, officer\u2019s and crew quarters and other spaces not available for carrying passengers or freight. Net registered tonnage is usually referred to as registered tonnage or net tonnage. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Net Tonnage</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - The volumetric cargo capacity of a ship expressed on the basis of 100 cubic feet to the ton. On passenger vessels it also includes space used by passengers. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">OBQ (On Board Quantity)</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - The material remaining in vessel tanks, void spaces, and/or pipelines prior to loading. On-board quantity includes water, oil, slops, oil residue, oil/water emulsions, sludge, and sediment. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">OCIMF </span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">\u2013 The oil companies\u2019 international marine forum is an organization of oil companies that own or operate ships.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Outage (Ullage)</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - The depth of the space in a tank not occupied by oil. Same as ullage. It is measured from the flange of the ullage hole to the surface of the oil. Also the space left in a petroleum product container to allow for expansion as a result of temperature changes during shipment and use. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Out-Turn Certificate</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - A document issued by the receivers of cargo indicating the amount of cargo <a href=\"\" name=\"P\"><b><i><span style=\"color: maroon;\">P</span></i></b></a><b><i><o:p></o:p></i></b></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Panamax</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - The maximum size ship that can fit through the Panama Canal in terms of width, length and draft generally about 80,000dwt. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Plimsoll Mark</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - The mark on the side of a classed vessel which indicates its safe load lines at varying seasonal conditions. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Port Charges</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - General term which includes charges and dues of every nature assessed against the vessel or its cargo in a port. It usually includes harbor dues, tub boat charges, pilotage fees, custom house fees, consular fees, etc. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Port State</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> \u2013 A state that has ports to which ships call. The port state makes regulations the calling ships must adhere to. The port state control is the controlling authority of the port state on shipping such as the coast guard or naval authorities.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Port Time (Two Types)</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> \u2013 1) Seabuoy to Seabuoy - The time elapsed between the vessel\u2019s passing the port\u2019s seabuoy upon entrance to re-passing it upon exit. It includes time for steaming in and out of berth, delays, hose connections, anchorage time, clearing and loading or unloading time. 2) Port to Port - Includes only time for delays, hose connections, anchorage time, clearing and loading or unloading time. Use must be consistent with voyage mileage basis. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Portable Measurement Unit (PMU)</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - A device designed to measure the ship\u2019s cargo when its tanks are closed to the atmosphere. It is used in conjunction with a vapor control valve. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Portable Sampling Unit (PSU)</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - A device designed to sample the ship\u2019s cargo when its tanks are closed to the atmosphere. It is used in conjunction with a vapor control valve. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Pressure/Vacuum Valve (P/V Valve)</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - An automatic dual purpose valve, commonly fitted in the vent lines of tankers. When in the closed position, the function of this valve is to relieve either pressure or vacuum in a tank. When in the open position it allows the passage of air or vapor into and out of the tank. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Reducer</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">- A short section of pipe, having one end of smaller diameter than the other and having a flange on each end, for connecting a smaller hose or pipe to a pipe of constant diameter. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Restricted Measurement System</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> \u2013 A measurement system designed to measure the ship\u2019s cargo when its tanks are closed to the atmosphere. During measurements a minimum amount of cargo vapors might escape to the atmosphere<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 0in; margin-right: 38.85pt; margin-top: .4pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 0in; margin-right: 38.85pt; margin-top: .4pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">ROB (Remain on Board)</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - The material remaining in vessel tanks, void spaces, and/or pipelines after discharge. Remaining on board quantity includes water, oil, slops, oil residue, oil/water emulsions, sludge, and sediment. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Rogue Wave</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> \u2013 An ocean wave much larger than the current wave sequence. This wave may also be outside the current wave direction and may be 100 feet or more in height<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Routing</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - A complex of measures concerning routes aimed at reducing the risk of casualties; it includes traffic separation schemes, two-way routes, tracks, areas to be avoided, inshore traffic zones, and deep water routes. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Sag (Sagging)</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - The condition of a vessel caused by the unequal distribution of cargo. When a vessel loads too heavily in the center it causes a bending downward of the hull at the midships area. This can also be caused by the vessel working in heavy seas with large waves under each end and no support under the center of the ship. Sag is the opposite of Hog. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Sea Trials</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - A series of trials conducted by the builders during which the owner\u2019s representatives on board act in a consulting and checking capacity to determine if the vessel has met the specifications. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Seaworthiness</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - The sufficiency of a vessel in materials constructions, equipment, crew and outfit for the trade in which the it is employed. Any sort of disrepair to the vessel by which the cargo may suffer; overloading; untrained officers; may constitute a vessel unseaworthy. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Seaworthiness Certificate</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - A certificate issued by a classification society surveyor to allow a vessel proceed after she has me with a mishap that may have affected its seaworthiness. It is frequently issued to enable a vessel to proceed, after temporary repairs have been effected, to another port where permanent repairs are then carried out. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Short-Handed</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - Said of a vessel inadequately manned or without the regular number of men. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Sister Ships</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - Ships built on the same design. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Slops</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - A mixture of petroleum and water normally arising from tank washings. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Sludge</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - A mixture of petroleum and water, usually semi-solid, frequently containing sand and scale. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Special Survey</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - The survey requirement of a classification society that usually takes place every four years. At the special survey vital pieces of equipment are opened up and inspected by the classification surveyor. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Stem</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>To order or arrange for, e.g bunkers.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Submarine Loading Terminal</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - A terminal where loading is carried out by means of an offshore hose run along the sea bottom. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Suezmax</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> \u2013 The maximize size ship that can sail through the Suez canal generally considered to be between 150-200,000 DWT depending on ships dimensions and draft.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Tender (TO)</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - A master tenders his vessel when he advises the charterer or supplier that he is ready to load. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Time-Charter</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - A form of charter party wherein owner lets or leases his vessel and crew to the charterer for a stipulated period of time. The charterer pays for the bunkers and charges in addition to the hire. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Tonnage Tax</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> \u2013 Taxes, fees, harbor dues etc. paid on the vessel based on a tonnage calculation.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Topping-Off</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - 1) the operation of completing the loading of a tank to a required ullage. 2) Filling up cargo tanks which were only partially filled at the loading port because of port or canal draft restrictions. The filling up occurs outside the loading port via lightering activities, or at another loading port. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; tab-stops: 138.0pt; text-autospace: none;\"><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"color: black; font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: .05pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; tab-stops: 138.0pt; text-autospace: none;\"><b .05pt;\">i</span>s<span style=\"letter-spacing: .1pt;\">h</span>es<span style=\"letter-spacing: -.3pt;\"> </span>for<span style=\"letter-spacing: -.05pt;\"> </span><span style=\"letter-spacing: .05pt;\">T</span>a<span style=\"letter-spacing: .1pt;\">n</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -.05pt;\">k</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: .1pt;\">e</span>r<span style=\"letter-spacing: -.25pt;\"> </span>Po<span style=\"letter-spacing: .05pt;\">r</span>t<span style=\"letter-spacing: -.2pt;\"> </span><span style=\"letter-spacing: .1pt;\">P</span>e<span style=\"letter-spacing: .05pt;\">r</span>f<span style=\"letter-spacing: .1pt;\">o</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: -.1pt;\">r</span><span style=\"letter-spacing: .1pt;\">m</span>an<span style=\"letter-spacing: .05pt;\">c</span>e<span style=\"letter-spacing: -.6pt;\"> </span><span style=\"letter-spacing: .1pt;\">p</span>u<span style=\"letter-spacing: .05pt;\">r</span>po<span style=\"letter-spacing: .05pt;\">s</span>e<span style=\"letter-spacing: .05pt;\">s</span>.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Track</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - The recommended direction or path to be followed when proceeding between pre-determined position. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Traffic</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - Movement of shipping. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Traffic Lane</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - An area within definite limits inside which one-way traffic is established. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Traffic Separation Scheme</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - A scheme which separates traffic proceeding in opposite or nearly opposite directions by the use of a separation zone or line, traffic lanes or by other means. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Underwriter</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">- In marine insurance one who subscribes his name to the policy indicating his acceptance of the liability mentioned therein consideration for which he receives a premium. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Unseaworthiness</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - The states or condition of a vessel when it is not in a proper state of maintenance, or if the loading equipment or crew, or in any other respect is not ready to encounter the ordinary perils of sea. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Used Laytime</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - The amount of lay time that was taken by the vessel for loading and discharging on a voyage. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Vapor Control Valve (VCV)</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> \u2013 This valves is used in conjunction with closed and restricted measurement equipment to allow measurements in ship\u2019s tanks that are closed to the atmosphere. Once a portable measurement unit (PMU) is attached to the VCV, the valve is opened and the PMU\u2019s probe is dropped into the tank to perform the required measurements.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Vapor Recovery System (VRS)</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - Procedures and equipment for the collection of hydrocarbon vapors from vessel\u2019s tanks and the transfer to shoreside recovery equipment. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Vessel Experience Factor (VEF)</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - A factor based on the compilation of the history of the total calculated volume (TCV) vessel measurements, adjusted for on-board quantity (OBQ) or remaining on board (ROB), compared with the TCV shore measurements. This factor if developed according to the latest industry standards may be used to obtain a better ship shore comparison of volumes.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Vetting</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - The general process of approving a vessel for use.&nbsp; (From old English \"To Vet\" - to look at or review again.)&nbsp; Note: actual procedure varies from company to company. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Wall Wash Test</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - The procedure of introducing an appropriate liquid into a vessel\u2019s tank to test for hydrocarbon, color and other contaminants. This test is done by physically pouring the liquid down vessel\u2019s tank bulkheads and trapping a portion on filter paper. This test is also done on vessel\u2019s steam coils and sumps.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Watertight Door</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - A door so constructed that, when closed, it will prevent water under pressure from passing through.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Water/Cut Measurement</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - The procedure of locating the oil/water interface for the purpose of determining the volume of free water in a shore tank or vessel compartment. It is also used to refer to the line of demarcation of the oil/water interface.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Wedge Formula</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - A mathematical means to approximate small quantities of liquid and solid cargo and free water on board prior to loading and after discharge based on cargo compartment dimensions and vessel trim. The wedge formula is to be used only when the liquid does not touch all bulk heads of the vessel\u2019s tanks.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Wedge Table</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - A pre-calculated vessel table based on the wedge formula and displayed much like the vessel\u2019s usual innage/ullage tables. These tables, however, are for small quantities (on- board quantities, remaining on board) when the cargo or free water does not touch all bulkheads of the vessel tank.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Wipe Test</span></b><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"> - The procedure of physically wiping random interior areas and steam coils of vessel\u2019s tanks with absorbent white rags. This procedure is used to test the tank\u2019s coating for possible color contamination.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TTd87qHRWmI/AAAAAAAADDA/227JFNeshJw/s1600/capt+ajit+vadakayil.JPG\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TTd87qHRWmI/AAAAAAAADDA/227JFNeshJw/s1600/capt+ajit+vadakayil.JPG\" /></a></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">-------CAPT AJIT VADAKAYIL ( 28 YEARS IN COMMAND )<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</div>", "author": {"id": "14410812789424637654", "displayName": "Capt. line-height: 150%;\">After running some more I felt some pain on the right hand side of the chest. I knew it had something to do with the liver , NOT the heart. <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">So I went home early. My old nanny saw me, as said immediately that my eyes are dull and yellow.&nbsp;</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif; font-size: 12pt; , serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Later after examining the rice, she said \u201c You have Jaundice\u201d.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; line-height: 150%;\">Before my parents could get back from work, she went into the back yard , pulled out a plant and within 10 minuted made me drink a blackish green concoction.&nbsp;</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">She told me that it was a mashed herb by the name of Kizhar Nelli and milk. It was so bitter that I spat it out.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Later when my parents came back from office, they made the herb paste into a small ball and made me swallow it with milk as a chaser.&nbsp;</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">I went to sleep. The next two days I did NOT go to school, as the right hand side of my chest still pained. I just ate curd and rice. The arm pits of my white uniform shirt had a tinge of yellow\u2014I was shown this by my mother. <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The third day I was back in school. I started playing soccer again after a week.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">This herb was in great demand by the Pharaohs of Egypt and the Kings of Palestine. Of course they could NOT grow it in their countries as this plant requires special soil, pollination &nbsp;and tropical weather.&nbsp;</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><br />\n</span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">Later in 4100 BC &nbsp;it was compiled and abridged by Narada the sage to 12000 verses.</span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><br />\n</span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">The laws were more of a code of ethics than legislative laws. There were NO severe punishments and the higher castes got punished more. Hammurabi's maritime laws for sea trade are lifted from&nbsp;laws formulated and adapted by sailors from Kerala, India.</span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><br /></span>\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><br />\n</span><br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TTcY4Kabn5I/AAAAAAAADB0/ePiKKN16Q8Y/s1600/images+%25283%2529.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TTcY4Kabn5I/AAAAAAAADB0/ePiKKN16Q8Y/s1600/images+%25283%2529.jpg\" /></span></a></div>\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><br />\n</span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">Manu received the eternal truths from Brahma , as he was a seer.</span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><br />\n</span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">At the Taxila university in 3000 BC, 10500 seats for world students were available as long as they were more than the age of 16. Students came from as far as Mesopotamia, Greece, Syria, Arabia , Russia, Thailand and China.</span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><br /></span>\n<br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><br />\n</span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">The laws Manu Smriti deals with epistemology, dialectics, metaphysics, empiricism , reason , truths, patience, forgiveness, self control, honesty, control of senses and sanctity.</span><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; The horoscope gives the navagrahas and rashis. <span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;</span>For Sri Rama of Ramayana who fought with Ravana in 4300 BC, his horoscope gives</span></span><span style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , &quot;serif&quot;;\"> <span class=\"apple-style-span\"><span style=\"color: black; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;\">position of different planets vis-a-vis zodiac constellations and nakshatras (visible stars) were: i) Sun in Aries; ii) Saturn in Libra; iii) Jupiter in Cancer; iv) Venus in Pisces; v) Mars in Capricorn; vi) Lunar month of Chaitra; vii) Ninth day after no moon; viii) Lagna as Cancer (cancer was rising in the east); ix) Moon on the Punarvasu (Gemini constellation &amp; Pllux star). max-width: 36px;\" /></div>\n<div class=\"comment-block\" style=\"font-size: 16px; margin-left: 48px; position: relative;\">\n<div class=\"comment-header\" style=\"margin: 0px 0px 8px;\">\n<cite class=\"user\" style=\"font-style: normal; font-weight: bold;\"><a href=\"https://www.blogger.com/profile/14410812789424637654\" rel=\"nofollow\" style=\"color: #888888; text-decoration-line: none;\">Capt. WHICH WAS OWNED BY THE CALICUT KING ( MY HOMETOWN)..<br /><br />Manu wrote 10,300 years ago --\u201c All the people on earth should learn their respective practices from a Brahmin born in that land of Brahmarisihidesa \u201d..<br /><br />JUST BECAUSE VEDAS WERE WRITTEN 7000 YEARS AGO--IT DOES NOT MEAN THERE WERE NO TEXTS BEFORE THAT..<br /><br />THIS IS BECAUSE ARYAVARTA ( PUNT/ SHEBA / OPHIR/ MALABAR/ ARYAVARTA / LAND OF GODS / BRAHMARISHIDESA ) WAS PART OF THE DANAVA CIVILIZATION-WHICH PRECEDED THE VEDIC CIVILISATION BY SEVERAL MILLINIUMS..<br /><br /><span style=\"color: red;\">http://ajitvadakayil.blogspot.com/2017/05/land-of-punt-ophir-and-sheba-is-north.html</span><br /><br />Brahmavarta area is credited to be Abode of Gods and was described as a land filled with Aryans.. Ajit Vadakayil</a></cite><span class=\"icon user blog-author\" style=\"background-image: url(&quot;data:image/png; background-repeat: no-repeat; display: inline-block; font-weight: bold; height: 18px; margin: 0px 0px -4px 6px; width: 18px;\"></span><span class=\"datetime secondary-text\" style=\"margin-left: 6px;\"><a href=\"https://ajitvadakayil.blogspot.com/2019/02/mistakes-deliberate-or-inadvertant-in.html?showComment=1549200842429#c4227901023722165533\" rel=\"nofollow\" style=\"color: #888888; text-decoration-line: none;\">February 3, 2019 at 7:04 PM</a></span></div>\n<div class=\"comment-content\" style=\"margin-bottom: 8px; text-align: justify;\">\nCONTINUED FROM 1--<br /><br /><span style=\"color: red;\">http://ajitvadakayil.blogspot.com/2011/01/manu-first-law-maker-capt-ajit.html</span><br /><br />Sir William Jones wrote that the Hindus of Kerala must have been navigators in the age of the writing of the Law Code of Manu, because the Law Code of Manu mentions bottomry (The lending of money for marine insurance).<br /><br />A bottomry, or bottomage, is an arrangement in which the master of a ship borrows money upon the bottom or keel of it, so as to forfeit the ship itself to the creditor, if the money with interest is not paid at the time appointed at the ship's safe return.<br /><br />This occurs, for example, where the ship needs urgent repairs during the course of its voyage or some other emergency arises and it is not possible for the master ( ship captain ) to contact the owner to arrange funds, allowing the master to borrow money on the security of the ship or the cargo by executing a bond. Where the ship is hypothecated, the bond is called a bottomry bond.<br /><br />The Code of Hammurabi describes a form of bottomry which is a risk transferring technique. A bottomry would be taken, but the repayment would be contingent on the ship successfully completing the voyage. This is more like a catastrophe bond than traditional insurance. In traditional insurance, you pay premiums and receive a benefit on the risk event. With bottomry and catastrophe bonds, you receive a loan up front and only pay it back with a premium if the risk event doesn't occur.<br /><br />CHANAKYA , THE ARYAN , HAD WRITTEN ABOUT SHIPPING LAWS AND MARINE INSURANCE LAWS IN HIS ARTHASHASTRA..<br /><br />my revelations now come to&nbsp;<span style=\"color: red; font-size: large;\"><b>59.38%</b></span><br /><br />When it reaches 97% the COLLECTIVE TWATS AND BALLS of this planet will go TRRRRRRRRRRRRR in resonance ..<br /><br />capt ajit vadakayil<br />..</div>\n</div>\n</li>\n<li class=\"comment\" id=\"c4227901023722165533\" style=\"border-bottom: 0px; It was one of the first logs in which the recorder was placed on board the ship rather than being part of the rotor. The Cherub Mark III series proved to be very successful and was produced in great numbers between 1930 and 1994..<o:p></o:p></i></span></div><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TTax9z_qpDI/AAAAAAAADBA/tGUF0nLro8Y/s1600/images+%25281%2529.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TTax9z_qpDI/AAAAAAAADBA/tGUF0nLro8Y/s1600/images+%25281%2529.jpg\" /></a></div><div style=\"margin: 0in 0in 12pt;\"><span style=\"color: black;\"><i><br />\n</i></span></div><br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span class=\"apple-style-span\"><i><span style=\"color: black; font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 115%;\">Made by Thomas Walker &amp; Son, Ltd of Birmingham, England whose name is synonymous with patent logs.&nbsp; It features a self contained&nbsp; instrument head&nbsp;with a&nbsp;distance measuring calculator which was mounted on the vessel's taffrail. The&nbsp;instrument section has a white porcelain&nbsp;face, and three analog counters with black Arabic numbers&nbsp;for distance run.&nbsp;A very large spinner or fish is trailed in the water behind the ship and its rotation is transmitted to the counter by means of a line (not included).</span><o:p></o:p></i></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span class=\"apple-style-span\"><i><span style=\"color: black; font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 115%;\"><br />\n</span></i></span></div><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TTayFVR3MhI/AAAAAAAADBE/PAFuzt-OZLs/s1600/images+%25283%2529.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TTayFVR3MhI/AAAAAAAADBE/PAFuzt-OZLs/s1600/images+%25283%2529.jpg\" /></a></div><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TTayJbSOxqI/AAAAAAAADBI/O6_yXOLUTLg/s1600/CHERUBTRADMK300+003.JPG\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TTayJbSOxqI/AAAAAAAADBI/O6_yXOLUTLg/s1600/CHERUBTRADMK300+003.JPG\" /></a></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span class=\"apple-style-span\"><span style=\"color: black; font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 115%;\"><i><br />\n</i></span></span></div><div style=\"margin: 0in 0in 12pt;\"><span style=\"color: black;\"><i>This instrument is a recorder for determining distance travelled and thus ship\u2019s speed. It is made of brass with a ceramic dial, with the main scale marked from 0 to 100 miles and two inset dials marked from 0 to 1000 miles and 0 to 1 mile. It has a fixing plate, on which it can turn, with which it would have been attached to a suitable part of the ship, typically the taffrail, the rail at the stern of a ship. As a result, this type of log was often called a taffrail log. The recorder would have been connected to a rotor that was towed behind the ship. The revolutions of the rotor registered on the indicator, thus measuring the distance travelled. For this model, 900 revolutions of the rotor registered as 1 nautical mile.</i><o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"margin: 0in 0in 12pt;\"><span style=\"color: black;\"><i><span class=\"apple-style-span\"><span style=\"color: black; font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 115%;\">We have satisfied customers in Australia, Austria, Belgium, Bermuda, Canada, Chile, China, Denmark, England, Finland, France, Germany, Holland, Ireland, Israel, Italy, Japan, Kuwait, Mexico, New Zealand, Norway, Nova Scotia, Saudi Arabia, Scotland, Singapore, Spain, Sweden, Thailand, USVI and the Eastern Caribbean</span></span></i></span></div><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TTax0J8YE8I/AAAAAAAADA4/gFcMPMCM5h4/s1600/images.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TTax0J8YE8I/AAAAAAAADA4/gFcMPMCM5h4/s1600/images.jpg\" /></a></div><div style=\"margin: 0in 0in 12pt;\"><span style=\"color: black;\"><i><br />\n</i></span></div><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TTd-weAJpZI/AAAAAAAADDI/879WMUutsJI/s1600/images+%25281%2529.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TTd-weAJpZI/AAAAAAAADDI/879WMUutsJI/s1600/images+%25281%2529.jpg\" /></a></div><br />\nCAPT AJIT VADAKAYIL<br />\n..</div>", "author": {"id": "14410812789424637654", "displayName": "Capt.
