An administrator ex-surgeon , who has not lifted the scalpel for 30 years , will never ever try to brow-beat or bulldoze a surgeon who does a brain operation job daily, with 100% success. This happens only with sailors.<br />\n<br />\nT<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: red;\">HIS POST IS ABOUT TURN BUCKLES AND BOTTLE SCREWS--</span><br />\n<br />\nOnce i attended a company seminar in a 7 star hotel , and the Dutch Technical director was telling a group of 200 Masters, Chief officers and Chief Engineers , about how a container ship lost their containers as the lashings were lose.<br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TTae_kWF_1I/AAAAAAAADAo/YVaemYYGbto/s1600/images+%25285%2529.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TTae_kWF_1I/AAAAAAAADAo/YVaemYYGbto/s1600/images+%25285%2529.jpg\" /></a></div><br />\nAnd then his cure and prevention rolled into one moronic solution was to keep checking and tightening the container lashing turnbuckles every 12 hours. He went on and on--literally frothing from the mouth--<br />\n<br />\nWhen he had got all in agreement , I got up , a cordless mike was thrust into my hand-- as when Capt Vadakayil speaks you get nothing but the NAKED TRUTH-- it must be loud and clear.<br />\n<br />\ni said - \" If a container turnbuckle is tightened it remains there, without loosening itself &nbsp;for the next 1000 years\" .<br />\n<br />\nthere was shocked silence -- i could see the MD had broken into a wry smile as he knew , that Vadakayil would take it to the logical bitter end.<br />\n<br />\nIt was time to lie back and enjoy, what is inevitable.<br />\n<br />\nhere is a gist of what i told him--the blow by blow account may be embarrassing to read--<br />\n<br />\nwhat is a nut and a bolt? how does the nut remain in position after tightening?<br />\n<br />\nIt is about elasticity of the steel bolt. This is why washer rings are used , in the absence of CHECK NUTS.<br />\n<br />\nThis is why the Japanese Kosaka &nbsp;Deepwell Pumps came a cropper. Their impeller was secured by stainless steel bolts and nuts. This usually worked lose with disastrous effects.<br />\n<br />\nThe Framo deepwell pump, understood this. They used nylon single use bolts and nylon washers. The impeller will NOT work lose.<br />\n<br />\nSo this means if if tighten a bottle screw, what you do is to bring two ends closer. Like when you &nbsp;tie your pyjamas with a single overhand knot.<br />\n<br />\nNow you need to hold it in position. On your pyjama it will be another overhand knot to make a reef knot ( a granny knot by land lubbers ).. On a bottle screw this boils down to TIGHTENING THE CHECK NUT -- or inserting a spike so that it will not unwind.<br />\n<br />\nAnother option would be to introduce friction on the worms by degreasing and putting a tough layer of paint. This is why an old rusted nut and bolt remains tight despite all vibration.<br />\n<br />\nSo, when you tighten a nut on a blot, the bolt elongates and keeps the nut in place. On a water tight door with dogs , the supple packing pushed the door outwards like a spring and holds the dogs in place. If the packing is hard on main decks you must change the packing, as it is this suppleness which keeps the door in place.<br />\n<br />\nA CHECK NUT IS SELF TIGHTENING IN VIBRATION. IT IS NOTHING BUT A SIMILAR NUT PUT OPPOSITE (OR ULTA AS WE INDIANS TERM IT.)<br />\n<br />\nSo next time you go on board , check your anchor lashing bottle screw, If it does not have a check nut replace it.<br />\n<br />\nOn chemical tankers we do NOT trust any nut and bolt system , unless it has a check nut. When i go for delivery of chemical tankers i insist that steam coil clamp nuts and bolts must have a check nut. Or very soon they will work loose and damage the sump impeller.<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TTafY7ugv4I/AAAAAAAADAs/iHn39aIQKd4/s1600/images+%25286%2529.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TTafY7ugv4I/AAAAAAAADAs/iHn39aIQKd4/s1600/images+%25286%2529.jpg\" /></a></div><br />\nOn brand new Japanese ships , they provide small stainless steel silver bottle screws , to secure the cabin chairs in rolling. These worms/ threads &nbsp;do NOT have any friction value and with every roll they loosen. After the first bad weather, all these fancy useless bottle screws with be lying here and there in pieces.<br />\n<br />\nOn my chemical tanker--i do NOT allow greasing of butter worth port butterfly nuts . When my ship carries Sulphuric acid or MEG FG, and if the tank cleaning port does not have check nuts , i get a light coat of epoxy paint applied on the threads AFTER tightening it. &nbsp;Only STUPID chemical chief officers use Silicon gun.<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TTacTZVu30I/AAAAAAAADAY/MrbjrlJ0amw/s1600/download+%25282%2529.JPG\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TTacTZVu30I/AAAAAAAADAY/MrbjrlJ0amw/s1600/download+%25282%2529.JPG\" /></a></div><br />\nLESSON: &nbsp;So, what makes the nut remain there after tightening? the FRICTION afforded by the elastic pull of the elongated steel bolt , and the compressed soft metal washer. If not, use another nut reverse to make a check nut, which is self tightening in vibrations &nbsp;.<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TTadmxv7sCI/AAAAAAAADAc/kHeaU6wguJU/s1600/images+%25282%2529.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TTadmxv7sCI/AAAAAAAADAc/kHeaU6wguJU/s1600/images+%25282%2529.jpg\" /></a></div>The above <span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"background-color: yellow; font-size: large;\">check nut with lever</span> can be tightened manually or with a small hammer.<br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TTab7iGND7I/AAAAAAAADAM/lAppDR9JRo8/s1600/images+%252810%2529.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TTab7iGND7I/AAAAAAAADAM/lAppDR9JRo8/s1600/images+%252810%2529.jpg\" /></a></div><br />\nCAPT AJIT VADAKAYIL ( 28 years in command )<br />\n..", "author": {"id": "14410812789424637654", "displayName": "Capt. Ajit Vadakayil", "url": "https://www.blogger.com/profile/14410812789424637654", "image": {"url": "//4.bp.blogspot.com/-QSnd-Z8F7Kc/XFtPudWdwlI/AAAAAAABfq4/vxrkFOO7Iu8Mf6-OaPgw6FPpRDSmMgLdgCK4BGAYYCw/s35/capt%25252BajitC%25252Bvadakayil.JPG"}}, "replies": {"totalItems": "2", "selfLink": "https://www.googleapis.com/blogger/v3/blogs/3564735312144269387/posts/5818582656082550314/comments"}}, {"kind": "blogger#post", "id": "7765911948248834307", "blog": {"id": "3564735312144269387"}, "published": "2011-01-19T12:11:00+05:30", "updated": "2015-04-09T19:28:12+05:30", "etag": "\"iHf3yWDE_geBgZ8U7rgZ_xuTeAQ/dGltZXN0YW1wOiAxNDI4NTg3ODkyNjI3Cm9mZnNldDogMTk4MDAwMDAK\"", "url": "http://ajitvadakayil.blogspot.com/2011/01/freezing-weather-precautions-on.html", "selfLink": "https://www.googleapis.com/blogger/v3/blogs/3564735312144269387/posts/7765911948248834307", "title": "FREEZING WEATHER PRECAUTIONS ON CHEMICAL TANKERS  --CAPT AJIT VADAKAYIL", "content": "<div dir=\"ltr\" style=\"text-align: left;\" trbidi=\"on\">\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TTaHfm8tnSI/AAAAAAAADAA/RSbXzpnRTNg/s1600/images.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TTaHfm8tnSI/AAAAAAAADAA/RSbXzpnRTNg/s1600/images.jpg\" height=\"300\" width=\"400\" /></a></div>\n<br />\n<em><span style=\"color: blue;\">Here in the picture below , you can see my ship (&nbsp;Vishva Pallav in 1983 )&nbsp;, negotiating sea-ice, in Chaleur Bay Canada, without ice class or ice bow.&nbsp; I was on bridge for 3 days continiously, sitting next to the telegraph, with my wife bringing my toothpaste and brush on bridge in the morning. Till then she used to think a Captain's job is a bed of roses-- all wine and song and travel.</span></em><br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-nFcGpQ2nxDg/TrpqvsmTq9I/AAAAAAAAH14/1k6IwYCBnx8/s1600/56.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-nFcGpQ2nxDg/TrpqvsmTq9I/AAAAAAAAH14/1k6IwYCBnx8/s320/56.jpg\" height=\"640\" width=\"524\" /></a></div>\n<br />\n<em><span style=\"color: blue;\">In the picture below you can see myself and my Chief Officer H Virendranath Hoige, planning an exit strategy from the Port of Belledune, considering the hull is NOT strengthened for ice and propeller is vulnerable.. In 1983, nobody made passage plans--we did it on our own.</span></em><br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-w87K4J8U-mM/TrprQ7ibV_I/AAAAAAAAH2A/2kT3HDZfVPo/s1600/55.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-w87K4J8U-mM/TrprQ7ibV_I/AAAAAAAAH2A/2kT3HDZfVPo/s320/55.jpg\" height=\"426\" width=\"640\" /></a></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"line-height: 22px;\"><b><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue; font-size: large;\">The most important thing while navigating in pack ice is that Master must realise that the pivoting fulcrum of the ship moves to the bow rake . &nbsp;So--when you give hard a port-- your stern moves to stbd, the bow remains there. Many inexperienced Masters have learnt this the hard way.&nbsp;</span> </b></span></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Freezing conditions require RISK ASSESSMENT form to be completed and sent to the office in advance.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; line-height: 150%;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: red; font-size: large;\">If you damage your ship in freezing weather, the reason is incompetence. </span></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-mr6AUzEo2MA/TrpsAb5fANI/AAAAAAAAH2I/IsdMkzUB7Pw/s1600/yyy.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-mr6AUzEo2MA/TrpsAb5fANI/AAAAAAAAH2I/IsdMkzUB7Pw/s400/yyy.jpg\" height=\"476\" width=\"640\" /></a></div>\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">If your ship has unltagged steam pipelines and if you are constantly shipping cold seas, you may not be able to keep the cargo fluid. The ship can take a cumulative list and sink.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">A chemical tanker has very low freeboard . The deck is cluttered with expensive tank attachments. Hardly any of them will be streamlined in case of rime. One devastating wave will do in the ship. Quite often the framo power pack is in the fore peak store. This means all hydraulic power is forward and if the ship has to even correct a list , or recirc cargo it may be difficult with the forecastle fully rimed. <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Hot salt water hose jets at high pressure is the best way to cut&nbsp; a swathe through the rime like hot knife through frozen butter ) . <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">If you have high VP cargoes forward whose PV vents get rimed, there will be structural damage. To prevent PV stack from freezing with rime, loose light canvas covers can be used. There are some cargoes like Stearic acid if they get frozen in the sample bottle the , white solid cargo rattles when shaken.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Don\u2019t breach institute warranty limits without informing the insurance dept\u2014just because \u201cocean routes advisory inadvertently advised you to breach it.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">All FW and unused steam deck pipes have to the examined on its own individual three dimensional merit and drained at its lowest point. This is Chief Officer\u2019s responsibility. If you do not do it with commonsense some valve body will crack. And be sure to change all river water FW ballast to salt water ballast.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">If your vessel is required to force ice in the C/P ensure you do some homework--- if you do not have the requisite ice experience. Damages to bows/ propeller can cost the company a fortune.</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-EDqYkxKKmOA/TrpsNslH0_I/AAAAAAAAH2Q/Mdgvw-PYotk/s1600/imagesCAH2EK7Z.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-EDqYkxKKmOA/TrpsNslH0_I/AAAAAAAAH2Q/Mdgvw-PYotk/s1600/imagesCAH2EK7Z.jpg\" height=\"149\" width=\"200\" /></a></div>\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"><b><i style=\"background-color: yellow;\">Basic precautions: Follow relevant ones only , using your commonsense.</i></b><o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">All space heaters for machinery on.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Antifreeze added to all radiators.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Header and hyd tanks oil heaters on.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Fresh water tanks heat or use adjacent heat <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Keep sufficient bunkers in double skin<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">LO and HO purifiers to run continuously.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Stern tube cooling water tank slack.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">DO filters cleaned more often to remove wax formation.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Maintain hotwell temperature for boiler<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Change over to partial sea water recirc of full ballast tank recirc for cooling water.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Ensure air vents of ballast tanks are clear. It hardly takes a kilo of pressure to burst the tank.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Steam trace sensitive pipelines. Have sufficient copper tubes and thermal lagging.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Open steam to DO settling and service tanks. Maintain temp at 40 deg C.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Drain OWS<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Bow thruster hyd oil heater put on 24 hrs before use.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Comply with machinery cold start recommendations in manual to prevent starting torque damage.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Keep steam injection hoses ready.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Open steam to sea chests and overboard as required.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Monitor suction/ dischg pressure gauges of SW pumps and inject steam if signs of ice is noticed.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Put up caution notices at local and remote starting points of various pumps whose drains are open.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Use plastic sheets to protect electrical equipment from condensation.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Note down how often the hydrophore cuts in cuts out. If it runs continuously investigate.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Isolate and drain all coolers of hyd systems.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Drain deck FW lines<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Shut off veg room / lobby cooling and use portable heaters to maintain to +5 deg C.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Keep only low sea suction open .<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Run clear view screens continuously.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Run radar scanners continuously<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Keep ready salt, shovels, hammers, crowbars, fire axes, blow lamps etc ready.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">It may be necessary to open manholes of ballast tanks while deballasting, ballasting.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Parcel sensitive pipes like bridge wash <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Inlet valves for draft gauges to be closed.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Keep all bilges dry<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Heat the accommodation interior. Do not open doors unnecessarily and allow heat to escape.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Drain all foam lines<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Blow and remove water from&nbsp; cargo heating coils of empty tanks.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Take sounding of peak tanks 3 times a day.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Grease PV floating lips, the mesh may get choked.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Critical pipes paint silver to retain the heat.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Bridge window wash cold water pipe cut off. Use only hot water. Run wiper blades slowly to avoid freezing of moving parts<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Reduce rudder limit to 10 degrees on auto pilot .<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">For detecting bergy bits use radar on continuous trails and small range.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">In pack ice use suez canal light.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">If you put silver foil&nbsp; inside your helmet or else where the body heat is retained.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Work with you back to the freezing wind.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Leave one hydrant open on the lowermost exposed deck.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Leave DO DB tanks slack.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Recirc hyd oil via thermal bypass.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Do not use steam hose to clear rime from Polypropylene hawsers on drum, cover with canvas..<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Make sure all sensitive moving parts are greased liberally including winch handles, drain cocks and compressed air valves.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Drill holes on external spindle protection sleeves of manual valves.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Obtain phone/ fax/ telex/ email ID\u2019s of local ice authorities.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Keep the ballast water level of wing tanks two feet below sea level.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">In case of boiler breakdown ensure there is enough DO.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Do not use bow thruster in ice.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Use artic grade HSD in the life boats \u2013if they are open.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">There is a possibility that the hyd relief valve of the steering will lift.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">When turning in pack ice remember that the sides of the vessel are weak.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Ensure that the propeller immersion is sufficient in pack ice\u2014especially if the vsl is calling to dischg.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Ice navigation is the sole discretion of the master in consultation with ice authorities.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Blow water off compressed air line from the lowest point. Use dehumidifier in engine room. Blow whistle regularly in snow.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Cold start spray must be available in life boats.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">In freezing rain the bridge portholes can get translucent/ opaque. It may be necessary to use portable heaters on bridge front glasses which do not have inbuilt heating.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Fill sounding pipes with antifreeze ( HO pipes with DO )<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Make air coupling for sounding pipes<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">No recirc of air in the engine room must be allowed<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Circulate fresh water systems<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Maintain small flow of water through the sanitary system<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Install a jumper line between supply and return of steam pipes.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Have more than usual bunkers and FW<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">In case you are rotating winches ensure greasing is done every 12 hours.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Frequent inspections to look for ruptured pipes.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Life boat engine water drained and space created for adding antifreeze.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Steering gear header tank heater on.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Stern tube cooling water tank slack.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Flow of cold air to machinery spaces to be reduced ( less fans and less dampers ) in the E/R by short circuiting air path between the skylight and the inlet vent.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Monkey island deck coated with silver to keep wheel house warm and comfortable. Use portable heaters o bridge<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Funnel flaps shut when warranted to protect boiler and economizer.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Try out whistles frequently.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">When vsl enters ice, log down the time and inform E/R.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Special briefing for bridge watch keepers and lookout men. How to identify old ice ridges and hummocks. Master on bridge all the time while in pack ice. Hence the necessity to pace himself like a marathon runner. Dropping out on reasons of fatigue before job completion means expensive damage or getting beset for a few days.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Officers to understand the concept of ship finding for itself path of least resistance with rudder amid ship.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Give wide berth to other ships in pack ice.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Freezing spray avoided by reducing speed / altering course. Keep Suez canal search light ready for night navigation through pack ice. If ship gets stuck use aft search light too.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Keep to beaten track in pack ice. Otherwise ice breakers who are short on patience will ignore you when stuck.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Use white coloured long johns and socks to preserve body heat. Make sure neck is not exposed.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">If you feel numbness on cheeks and nose go indoors and get warm.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">In case of boiler breakdown , have sufficient DO.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Keep bown down to keep ice off the thruster tunnel.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">On unlagged steam lines it is all right to have a small steam leak to act as relief during hammer.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Procure Halogen lamps for use in spaces which do not have space heater.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">The wheelhouse atmosphere must be warm and dry . not warm and moist. Otherwise the inner wheelhouse glass with get frozen and opaque. Avoid using kettle in the wheel house.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">The forepeak tank must be filled above water level to act as a shock absorber.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">It will be advisable to determine the melting point of heated cargoes yourself by using sample bottles. This will avoid unnecessary overheating on bad weather days with unlagged pipelines.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Chief officer must record how may turns the steam coil return valves are open for heated cargoes. Stow high MP cargoes aft.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Prolonged steam hammer even at night means bad management. <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">If you allow steam to return to E/Room from tankheating coils ,not water, your ship may deplete her safe bunker reserves<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Remember black colour is a good radiator and a good absorber of heat. Silver colour on the contrary is a bad radiator and a bad absorber.</span><span lang=\"EN\" style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<tt><span lang=\"EN\" style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">The most serious problem experienced during navigation in pack ice has been damage to propeller caused by astern movements.The trailing edge of a propeller has the thinnest section and is unable to withstand the additional forces when it suddenly becomes the leading edge running in ice. Physical edge damage and deformation/bending within the thinner section will cause severe overload of engine often accompanied by heavy vibrations.<o:p></o:p></span></tt></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<tt><span lang=\"EN\" style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">At sea the fresh water tank for stern tube cooling should be checked daily that it remains liquid and in port it should be drained out and refilled prior engine operation.<o:p></o:p></span></tt></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<tt><span lang=\"EN\" style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Sufficient air space should be left in each FW tank. Upper manhole may be opened in order to break any ice that forms. Circulating of fresh water may be considered if freezing in tank or supply lines occurs.<o:p></o:p></span></tt></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<tt><span lang=\"EN\" style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Bunker line steam tracing should be used if fitted. Ensure settling and service tanks are full on arrival and maintain temperatures. Transfer if necessary from heated bunker tank and drain fuel line on completion.<o:p></o:p></span></tt></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<tt><span lang=\"EN\" style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">In port one steering gear pump may be left running and rudder swung occasionally.<o:p></o:p></span></tt></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<tt><span lang=\"EN\" style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Resistance reading should be taken before starting any motor especially steering motors, deck machinery motors and those located at engine room lower level.<o:p></o:p></span></tt></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<tt><span lang=\"EN\" style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Apply heat to M/E to prevent freezing. Allow extra time to heat to minimum inlet &nbsp;temperatures before manoeuvring.<o:p></o:p></span></tt></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<tt><span lang=\"EN\" style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Control air system drain regularly and every two hours in the period prior to departure.<o:p></o:p></span></tt></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<tt><span lang=\"EN\" style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Protect LB water rations<o:p></o:p></span></tt></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<tt><span lang=\"EN\" style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Keep all batteries fully charged.</span></tt></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TTaHFoIHiJI/AAAAAAAAC_8/mvrggqxx038/s1600/capt+ajit+vadakayil.JPG\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TTaHFoIHiJI/AAAAAAAAC_8/mvrggqxx038/s1600/capt+ajit+vadakayil.JPG\" /></a></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-bCQ7IpPCxeg/TrpslnhQJvI/AAAAAAAAH2Y/h_osP6UtHDQ/s1600/ccc.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-bCQ7IpPCxeg/TrpslnhQJvI/AAAAAAAAH2Y/h_osP6UtHDQ/s1600/ccc.jpg\" /></a></div>\n<span lang=\"EN\" style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Ensure the hyd system does not have water contamination. Use sand at slippery areas.<br />\n<i style=\"mso-bidi-font-style: normal;\"><br />\nNote: </i></span><i style=\"mso-bidi-font-style: normal;\"><span style=\"color: black; font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Freezing Point of FW is 0 deg C and sea water is -1.91 deg C</span></i></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-TBjTQC-luyA/TrpstDvaR8I/AAAAAAAAH2g/BDf3n7K0pJU/s1600/rrr.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-TBjTQC-luyA/TrpstDvaR8I/AAAAAAAAH2g/BDf3n7K0pJU/s1600/rrr.png\" /></a></div>\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">-------CAPT AJIT VADAKAYIL<i style=\"mso-bidi-font-style: normal;\"><span style=\"color: black;\"><o:p></o:p></span></i></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span lang=\"EN\" style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n<br />\n</span><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;, serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<br /></div>\n</div>\n", "author": {"id": "14410812789424637654", "displayName": "Capt. font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><i>This language is Sanskrit and is 11000 years old .&nbsp;</i></span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">This was the language Aryan Indian Emperor Vikramadiya used when he ruled from Jerusalem to Urals to Cambodia in 7000 BC.&nbsp;</span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">--pretty much the same way British Queen Victoria ruled all the Commonwealth countries and even the waves . The only difference is <span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"background-color: yellow;\">this man GAVE -- he did not TAKE -- or steal or vandalise or subvert or convert or ram down into unwilling throats</span>&nbsp;--</span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">Sanskrit is the mother of a lot of languages in the world.</span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\">This man was loved by all -- as he was a spreader of culture, medicine , astronomy, prayer, language and laws. &nbsp;He is the man who endorsed the power of the black meteorite stones at Mecca , Petra, &nbsp;Jerusalem, and far east temples till Cambodia. &nbsp;The below picture is a temple in Cambodia with Ramayana gods.</span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><br />\n</span><br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TTakDw5CaFI/AAAAAAAADA0/CtRfJtEpCT8/s1600/21-36.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><img border=\"0\" height=\"212\" src=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TTakDw5CaFI/AAAAAAAADA0/CtRfJtEpCT8/s320/21-36.jpg\" width=\"320\" /></span></a></div><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><i>The Petra black stone was stolen-- and then this civilization died -- as the sole reason of people staying there was just this powerful resonant stone. The same way the most important part of Kaaba is the black meteorite stone at the SE corner. These stones are surprisingly heavy for their size.</i></span></span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" tab-stops: list .25in; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><!--[if !supportLists]--><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\"><span style=\"mso-list: Ignore;\">1 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;</span></span><!--[endif]--><span style=\"color: #ff6600; font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\">Acids, Inorganic Non-oxidizing</span><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\"><span style=\"mso-tab-count: 1;\">&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; margin-left: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list .25in; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; margin-left: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list .25in; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\"><span style=\"mso-tab-count: 1;\"></span>&nbsp;&nbsp;generally nonflammable. Generally soluble in water with the release of hydrogen ions. The resulting solutions has pH's of less than 7.0. Acids neutralize<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>chemical bases<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>to form salts. Neutralization occurs as the base accepts hydrogen ions that the acid donates. Neutralization can generate dangerously large amounts of heat in small spaces.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Dilution in water may generate heat and sputtering. React with active metals to release hydrogen, a flammable gas.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Can initiate the polymerization of certain classes of organic compounds.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Reacts with cyanide compounds to release gaseous hydrogen cyanide. Generates flammable and/or toxic gases in contact with certain chemicals and strong reducing agents.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Often catalyze (increase the rate) of chemical reactions. Corrosive to tissue. Acid fumes irritate sensitive tissues such the eyes and respiratory system especially severely. Have a sour taste .Turns blue litmus red EXAMPLES - Hydrochloric acid, hydroiodic acid, hydrobromic acid, hydrofluoric acid, phosphoric acid.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-left: 0in; text-indent: -6pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-size: 15px; line-height: 17px;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\">2 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: red;\">Acids Inorganic&nbsp;</span></span><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-size: 15px; line-height: 17px;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: red;\">Oxidizing</span><span style=\"mso-tab-count: 1;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>Same as non oxidizing. Have significant ability as oxidizing agents. but that ability varies (for example, from high for nitric acid to low for sulfuric acid and most sulfonic acids). They can react with active metals, and also many less active metals, to dissolve the metal and liberate hydrogen and/or toxic gases.. Flammable and/or toxic gases are also often generated by their reactions with certain chemicals and <span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;</span>reducing agents. Often catalyze (increase the rate) of chemical reactions. EXAMPLES - nitric acid, perchloric acid, arsenic acid, chlorosulfonic acid, chromic acid, fluorosulfonic acid, chloric acid, nitrosulfuric acid, selenic acid, sulfurous acid.</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\">3<span style=\"mso-tab-count: 1;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style=\"color: #ff6600;\">Carboxylic Acids</span><span style=\"mso-tab-count: 1;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>Reasonably wide flammability limits. A moderate fire hazard. Most are moderately soluble in water. Even \"insoluble\" carboxylic acids may absorb enough water from the air and dissolve sufficiently in it to corrode steel. Like other acids, carboxylic acids may initiate polymerization reactions. Corrosive to tissue. Most carboxylic acids are solids at room temperature; formic, acetic, propanoic, and butanoic acids are liquids.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>EXAMPLES - Formic acid, acetic acid, oxalic acid, propionic acid, trichlorophenoxyacetic acid, benzoic acid, citric acid, fumaric acid, the fatty acids. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\">4<span style=\"mso-tab-count: 1;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style=\"color: #ff6600;\">Alcohols and Polyols</span><span style=\"mso-tab-count: 1;\">&nbsp;&nbsp; </span> Many alcohols are highly flammable . Especially dangerous are methanol and ethyl alcohol, because of their wide flammability limits. Polyols are generally combustible. Their general low volatility means that they are poorly flammable. Flammable and/or toxic gases are generated by the combination of these materials with alkali metals, nitrides, and strong reducing agents. They react with organic acids to form esters plus water. Oxidizing agents convert them to aldehydes or ketones. They exhibit both weak acid and weak base behavior. They may initiate the polymerization of isocyanates and epoxides. Alcohols and polyols vary widely in toxicity. Among the most toxic are methyl and allyl alcohol, which act as nervous system depressants. These materials are organic compounds. EXAMPLES - Ethyl alcohol, methanol, propanol, butanol, ethylene glycol, hexanol, allyl alcohol, amyl alcohol, benzyl alcohol, cyclopentanol, glycerol, isopropyl alcohol, isobutyl alcohol.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\">5<span style=\"mso-tab-count: 1;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style=\"color: #ff6600;\">Aldehydes</span><span style=\"mso-tab-count: 1;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span> Aldehydes are volatile liquids, and are highly flammable. Dangerous ones are formaldehyde, acetaldehyde, acrolein, crotonaldehyde, and other aldehydes that have wide flammability limits. Aldehydes are frequently involved in self-condensation or polymerization reactions. These reactions are exothermic; they are often catalyzed by acid. Aldehydes are readily oxidized to give carboxylic acids. Flammable and/or toxic gases are generated by the combination of aldehydes with some chemicals and strong reducing agents. Aldehydes can react with air to give first peroxo acids, and ultimately carboxylic acids. These autoxidation reactions are activated by light, catalyzed by salts of transition metals, and are autocatalytic (catalyzed by the products of the reaction). The addition of stabilizers (anti-oxid</span><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-size: 15px; line-height: 17px;\">ants) to shipments of aldehydes retards autoxidation. Aldehydes act by inhalation, by ingestion, and by contact with the skin. Their exact metabolic effect depends upon the route of exposure. Among the most toxic are acrolein and crotonaldehyde, which are known carcinogens. Aldehydes are known sensitizers for small populations of humans and serve to cause chemically induced allergic reactions. The effects of these reactions can be dramatic at rather low concentrations. The effects of formaldehyde and acetaldehyde have been well documented because these aldehydes are found in many synthetic products, such as clothing, insulation, and building products. EXAMPLES - Formaldehyde, butyraldehyde, acetaldehyde, benzaldehyde, crotonaldehyde, acrolein, propionaldehyde, pentanal, valeraldehyde.</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\">6<span style=\"mso-tab-count: 1;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style=\"color: #ff6600;\">Amides and Imides, Organic</span><span style=\"mso-tab-count: 1;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span> Compounds in this group are combustible. The products of their combustion include noxious NOx. <span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;</span>Organic amides react with azo and diazo compounds to generate toxic gases. Flammable gases are formed by the reaction of organic amides with strong reducing agents. Amides are very weak bases (weaker than water). Imides are less basic yet and in fact react with strong bases to form salts. That is, they can react as acids.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Low to moderate toxicity. They act by ingestion and by contact with the skin. Most amides are solids at room temperature (exception: formamide). Amides containing five carbon atoms or fewer are soluble in water. Amides are versatile chemicals that enter into many useful reactions, especially in the fertilizer industry. Polyamides are polymers . Proteins in foods are naturally occurring polyamides; Nylon is a synthetic polymer.EXAMPLES - Urea, acetamide, acrylamide, benzamide, caprolactam, formamide, dimethylformamide, phenylurea. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\">7<span style=\"mso-tab-count: 1;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style=\"color: #ff6600;\">Amines</span><span style=\"mso-tab-count: 1;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span> Amines are generally high-boiling liquids or solids at room temperature and are not highly flammable.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Amines are combustible. The combustion of amines yields noxious NOx. Amines are chemical bases. They neutralize acids to form salts plus water. These acid-base reactions are exothermic.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Flammable gaseous hydrogen is generated by amines in combination with strong reducing agents, such as hydrides.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Some are very poisonous; others are only slightly toxic. Many amines are skin irritants. Some amines are known sensitizers for small populations of humans and serve to cause chemically induced allergic reactions. The effects of such reactions can be dramatic at rather low concentrations. Amines are organic compounds derived from ammonia . Many amines have unpleasantly fishy or putrid odors.EXAMPLES - Methylamine, aniline, triethanolamine, hexamethylenetetramine, cyclohexylamine, xylidine, ethylaniline, pyridine, anisidine, diphenylamine, ethylenediamine. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\">8<span style=\"mso-tab-count: 1;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style=\"color: #ff6600;\">Azo, Diazo, and Azido Compounds and Organic Hydrazines, Organic</span><span style=\"mso-tab-count: 1;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span> Many Azo, Diazo, and Azido compounds are highly flammable/explosive (with flash points below 100 degrees F).<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Hydrazine and methylhydrazine are especially dangerous because of their low flash points and wide flammability limits. All compounds in this group give products that include noxious NOx. Many azides, especially the heavy metal azides, easily detonate by friction, shock, or heating.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Some materials in this group can detonate. This applies in particular to organic azides that have been sensitized by the addition of metal salts or strong acids. Toxic gases are formed by mixing materials of this class with acids, aldehydes, amides, carbamates, cyanides, inorganic fluorides, halogenated organics, isocyanates, ketones, metals, nitrides, peroxides, phenols, epoxides, acyl halides, and strong oxidizing or reducing agents. Flammable gases are formed by mixing materials in this group with alkali metals. Explosive combination can occur with strong oxidizing agents, metal salts, peroxides, and sulfides.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Acutely toxic by all routes of exposure. They are good oxidizing agents. EXAMPLES - Azidoacetaldehyde, azidoacetic acid, azidoacetone, aminophenylazobenzene, azobenzene, diazomethane, diazoacetonitrile, hydrazine, diazoacetaldehyde. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\">9<span style=\"mso-tab-count: 1;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style=\"color: #ff6600;\">Carbamates and Esters</span><span style=\"mso-tab-count: 1;\"> </span> Compounds in this group are high-boiling liquids . They are generally nonflammable, but are combustible. Combustion products include noxious NOx and carbon monoxide. Materials in this group are chemically similar to, but more reactive than amides. Like amides they form polymers such as polyurethane resins. Carbamates are incompatible with strong acids and bases, and especially incompatible with strong reducing agents such as hydrides. Flammable gaseous hydrogen is produced by the combination of active metals or nitrides with carbamates. Strongly oxidizing acids, peroxides, and hydroperoxides are incompatible with carbamates. Many carbamates are used as pesticides. These materials can be extremely toxic. They act by blocking the function of cholinesterase, an enzyme that is essential to the transmission of nerve impulses. Oral exposure is the principal concern. Absorption through the skin is slow, but dermal exposure must still be avoided because of the high toxicity. Compounds in this group are derivatives of carbamic acid (NH2COOH). The urethanes are alkyl carbamates, that is, esters of carbamic acid.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>EXAMPLES - Carbamic acid, ammonium carbamate, carbaryl, oxamyl, propoxur, urethane.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\">10<span style=\"color: #ff6600;\">Bases</span><span style=\"mso-tab-count: 1;\"> </span> Materials in this group are mostly nonflammable and non-combustible. - Compounds in this group are chemically similar to sodium hydroxide (NaOH) or sodium oxide (Na2O). They neutralize acids exothermically to form salts plus water. When soluble in water they give solutions having a pH greater than 7.0. Mixing these materials with water can generate troublesome amounts of heat as the base is dissolved or diluted.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Bases may initiate polymerization reactions in polymerizable organic compounds, especially<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>epoxides). They may generate flammable and/or toxic gases with ammonium salts, nitrides, halogenated organics, various metals, peroxides, and hydroperoxides. Materials of this group often serve as catalysts.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Corrosive to tissue. Solutions of bases have a bitter taste and a slippery feel; they turn red litmus blue.EXAMPLES - Sodium hydroxide, potassium hydroxide, ammonium hydroxide, barium hydroxide, barium oxide, beryllium hydroxide, calcium hydroxide, calcium oxide.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\">11<span style=\"color: #ff6600;\">Cyanides, Inorganic</span><span style=\"mso-tab-count: 1;\"> </span>Materials in this group are generally noncombustible. Cyanides are often flammable by chemical reaction with moisture or acid; they react readily to evolve flammable HCN. Heating inorganic cyanides to decomposition liberates toxic gases and flammable gases that include HCN if traces of moisture are present. Materials in this group react slowly with water to evolve gaseous hydrogen cyanide (HCN). Acids cause the rapid evolution of HCN; carbon dioxide from the air is sufficiently acidic to liberate HCN from solutions of cyanides.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Cyanides have been known to initiate polymerization reactions of epoxides. Cyanides form compounds with metal salts; heat and hydrogen production may accompany these reactions. Some cyanides can detonate when exposed to shock, heat, or friction. Many of these materials are corrosive to tissue and are extremely toxic by all routes of exposure. Cyanides bind hemoglobin in the blood, and many enzymes are inactivated in the presence of cyanide. Cyanogen chloride and bromide are lachrymators. Cyanides are used as pesticides and in chemical synthesis.EXAMPLES - Barium cyanide, calcium cyanide, copper cyanide, cyanogen chloride, hydrogen cyanide, lead cyanide, potassium cyanide, silver cyanide. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\">12<span style=\"color: #ff6600;\">Thiocarbamate Esters and Salt/Dithiocarbamate Esters and Salts</span><span style=\"mso-tab-count: 1;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span> Materials in this group are combustible. Poisonous gases are generated by the thermal decomposition of compounds of this class, including carbon disulfide, oxides of sulfur, oxides of nitrogen, hydrogen sulfide, ammonia, and methylamine. Many materials in this group slowly decompose in aqueous solution to form carbon disulfide and methylamine or other amines. Such decompositions are accelerated by acids. TOXICITY - The slow release of poisonous gases from hydrolysis of many compounds in this group requires the use of respirators during handling. Poisoning can also occur by ingestion and absorption through the skin. <span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;</span>These chemicals are used in the synthesis of polymers and in agriculture as pesticides, soil fumigants, and seed disinfectants.EXAMPLES - Cycloate, ethyl dithiocarbamate, ferbam, maneb, ethylenebisdithiocarbamate, metham sodium, nabam, thiram, sodium dimethyldithiocarbamate, thiobencarb, zineb,<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>zinc diethyldithiocarbamate. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\">13<span style=\"color: #ff6600;\">Esters</span><span style=\"mso-tab-count: 1;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span> Many esters are flammable or highly flammable.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>All are capable of being combustible and yield toxic gases such as carbon monoxide when burned. Some may spontaneously heat and ignite if stored wet and hot. Materials in this group react with acids to liberate heat along with alcohols and acids. Strong oxidizing acids may cause a vigorous reaction that is sufficiently exothermic to ignite the reaction products. Heat is also generated by the interaction of esters with caustic solutions. Flammable hydrogen is generated by mixing esters with alkali metals and hydrides.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Inhalation of the fumes from some esters irritates the mucous membranes. Esters have low to moderate toxicity via dermal and oral exposure. Some esters are used as flavoring agents in foodstuffs. Their names are derived from the names of the acid and alcohol from which they are synthesized. Esters include the edible fats and oils, which are mixed esters between the triol glycerol and fatty acids. Esters are prominent in the perfumery and flavoring industry. They are used to manufacture synthetic fibers such as polyester and plastics.EXAMPLES - Ethyl acetate, methyl acrylate, cyclohexyl acrylate, butyl propionate, butyl lactate, butyl formate, butyl acetate, benzyl acetate, amyl butyrate, amyl acetate, allyl acetate.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\">14<span style=\"color: #ff6600;\">Ethers</span><span style=\"mso-tab-count: 1;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span> Low-molecular-weight ethers are flammable gases (methyl ether) or liquids (methyl ethyl ether or ethyl ether) that can produce explosive mixtures when they evaporate and mix with air. Ethers form peroxides if exposed to oxygen or air<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>during storage; the ether peroxides can detonate with friction, shock, or heat, releasing enough energy to start a secondary fire in the unperoxidized ether.- Ethers tend to form unstable peroxides when exposed to oxygen. Ethyl, isobutyl, ethyl tert-butyl, and ethyl tert-pentyl ether are particularly hazardous in this respect. Ether peroxides can sometimes be observed as clear crystals deposited on containers or along the surface of the liquid. Ethers can act as bases. They form salts with strong acids . Ethers may react violently with strong oxidizing agents. Ethers<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>are moderately toxic. The lower-molecular weight ethers are powerful rapid-acting narcotics by inhalation. Toxic effects from these compounds are usually acute not chronic. The swallowing of one ounce of a liquid ether may be fatal. EXAMPLES - Phenyl ether, ethyl ether, allyl ethyl ether, anisidine, anisole, butyl methyl ether, butyl vinyl ether, diallyl ether, isopropyl ether, divinyl ether, methyl ether, isobutyl. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\">16<span style=\"color: #ff6600;\">Hydrocarbons, Aromatics</span><span style=\"mso-tab-count: 1;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span> Aromatic hydrocarbons are all combustible. The lightest members of this class, benzene and substituted benzenes, have high enough vapor pressures and low enough flash points to be vapor explosion hazards. Vigorous reactions, sometimes amounting to explosions, can result from the contact between these materials and strong oxidizing agents. They can react exothermically with bases . Many aromatic hydrocarbons are poisons by inhalation and irritants to the skin and eyes. Some are poisons by skin contact. Aromatic hydrocarbons are very often carcinogenic (benzene is an example). Compounds in this group contain the benzene nucleus. In benzene six carbon atoms form a ring maintained by alternating single and double bonds; each carbon atom is also bonded to a hydrogen atom. Aromatic hydrocarbons possess a single benzene nucleus with side-groups replacing one or more of the hydrogen atoms or in fused sets of two or more rings. They are common air contaminants.EXAMPLES - Benzene, toluene, naphthalene, pyrene, anthracene, chrysene, acenaphthylene, xylene, benzo[a]pyrene, biphenyl, cumene, fluorene, phenanthrene. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\">17<span style=\"color: #ff6600;\">Halogenated Organic Compounds</span><span style=\"mso-tab-count: 1;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span> The flammability of these materials is variable. The low-molecular-weight materials (gases and liquids) are generally dangerously flammable.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Simple aromatic halogenated organic compounds are very unreactive; halogenated aliphatic compounds are moderately or very reactive.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Halogenated acetylene compounds are unstable and should be treated as explosives. Low molecular weight haloalkanes are highly flammable and can react with some metals to form dangerously products. Low molecular weight haloalkenes are highly flammable, peroxidizable and may polymerize violently. They may react violently with aluminum. Materials in this group are incompatible with strong oxidizing and reducing agents. Also, they are incompatible with many amines, nitrides, azo/diazo compounds, alkali metals, and epoxides. Many halogenated hydrocarbons have moderate to high toxicity by inhalation. The brominated materials tend to be particularly toxic. Much of the toxicity is due to the fact that these substances are not metabolized, but persist and accumulate in fatty tissues (they tend to be fat-soluble). The combustion of chlorinated organic compounds may produce poisonous phosgene gas . Other materials formed by incomplete combustion are classes of chlorinated organic compounds, chlorodibenzodioxins and chlorodibenzofurans. These compounds cause cancer in laboratory tests. This class of compounds is extremely important in industry in the production of polymers, pesticides, and fire retardants.EXAMPLES - Vinyl chloride, vinylidene chloride, chlorobenzene, trichlorobenzene, polychlorinated biphenyls (PCBs), methylene chloride, chloroform, chloroisoprene, trichlorobenzene. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 115%; text-indent: -6.0pt;\"><span style=\"font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 115%;\">18<span style=\"color: #ff6600;\">Isocyanates and Isothiocyanates, Organic</span><span style=\"mso-tab-count: 1;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span> These materials usually have low vapor pressures and are non-flammable. All are combustible. They evolve poisonous gases such as HCN, NOx, SOx, and CO when they burn.
