font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Corrosive&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Having the quality of eating away or consuming by chemical action.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Covalent bond&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A chemical bond in which atoms of either like or unlike elements link by sharing electrons.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Cryogenic&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Matter at extremely low temperatures, usually approaching absolute zero (obtainable only by employing the liquefied gases hydrogen, helium, oxygen, and nitrogen).<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Deflagration&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Rapid, sharp combustion with sudden evolution of flame.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Delayed A hazard category that includes carcinogens and other hazardous chemicals that adversely affect a target organ. Such effects generally result from long-term exposure and are of long duration. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Deliquescent&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; The property of becoming liquid by absorbing moisture from the air.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Denature&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; The addition of a toxic material such as benzene or methyl alcohol (a denaturant) to ethyl alcohol to inhibit or prevent its use for human consumption.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Density&nbsp;&nbsp; The ratio of weight to volume of any substance<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Detergent&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp; A natural or synthetic agent that suspends emulsified oils, greases, and fats in solution and, by doing this, acts as a cleaning agent. Examples of detergents include soaps and various alcohols, sulfonated organics like dodecylbenzene, and various alkylates.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Detonation&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; The very rapid decomposition of an explosive material, which produces a rapidly-propagating, high-pressure wave traveling at supersonic speeds.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Dew point &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The temperature at which air is saturated with water.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Dispersion&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; The movement of molecules or finely divided particles through a gaseous or liquid medium. For example, the distribution of a toxic chemical cloud in the atmosphere.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Distillation&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; The process of separating a mixture of materials by heating and then condensing the resulting vapors. The separation is made possible by the inherent differences in boiling point among the individual mixture components (each can be distilled out of the mixture at a particular temperature).<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Efflorescent&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Tending to lose moisture to the air as shown by the formation of a powder on the surface.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Elastomer&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Any of a group of rubber-like polymers that have essentially the same properties as natural rubbers.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Electrolyte&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;  &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In a battery, the material that acts as a conductor of electric current between the dissimilar metal electrodes. These are ionically-bonded, inorganic salts that form ions in solution and thus increase electrical conductivity.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Electrons&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp; Negatively-charged elementary particles that have a very small mass. Electrons are components of all atoms; they are readily lost or gained by atoms. (See Ion.) The transfer and sharing (redistribution) of electrons among atoms is the basis of chemical change.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Electrophile&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A chemical reactant that tends to react at centers of negative charge.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Electroplating&nbsp;&nbsp; For corrosion protection or decorative purposes, an electrodeposition process that coats a surface with a thin film of metal (or plastic), by creating an electrolytic cell in which metal atoms are deposited on the cathode and the anode acts as the reservoir of ions in solution.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Emulsification&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp; Generally, either the dispersion of oil particles in water or water in oil. The emulsification process is relatively permanent, and may proceed with the help of an emulsification agent.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Endothermic&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A chemical reaction that must absorb heat from its surroundings in order to proceed. Contrast with exothermic, in which heat is produced by the forward reaction.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Enzyme&nbsp; Any of a number of complex proteins that act in extremely specific chemical reactions to accelerate reactions or catalyze a specific reaction. The rates of reaction are often many orders of magnitude faster than the rates for the same reaction at standard temperature and pressure conditions. All metabolic processes in living organisms are governed by enzymes.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">EPA&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; U. S. Environmental Protection Agency. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Exothermic&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A term used to describe the generation of heat from a chemical reaction. Contrast with endothermic, in which heat is taken in from the surroundings.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Explosion&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp; A chemical or physical process in which the rate at which energy is being generated exceeds its ability to escape to its surrounding environment. The hazards of an explosion can include a shock wave, especially near the point of explosion, and projectiles generated by the shock wave.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Explosive&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A material synthesized or mixed deliberately to allow the very rapid release of chemical energy. Also, a chemical substance that is intrinsically unstable and liable to detonate under conditions that might reasonably be encountered.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Extremely Hazardous Substances&nbsp;</span><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 13px; line-height: 17px;\">EHS)&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; EHS chemicals have been identified by the U.S. Environmental Protection Agency as particular toxic threats. They are listed under EPCRA in the appendices to 40 CFR \u00a7 355, Emergency Planning and Notification.</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 13px; line-height: 17px;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Fermentation&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; An energy-yielding reaction carried out in an anaerobic environment (without oxygen), catalyzed by enzymes (biochemical catalysts) and involving the decomposition of carbohydrates (sugars and starch) to form alcohols, carboxylic acids, and carbon dioxide.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Fire hazard&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A hazard category that includes chemicals described as flammable, combustible liquid, pyrophoric, or oxidizers <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Flammability&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A substance's tendency to ignite or take flame. Flammability is closely related to the volatility of a substance (and is not its relative ability to burn in the presence of oxygen with the evolution of heat).<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Flammability limits&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Or explosive limits. The lower flammability limit is the lowest concentration of a vapor in air that catches fire when exposed to a source of ignition. The upper flammability limit is the highest concentration of the vapor in air that catches fire when exposed to a source of ignition. The flash point and lower and upper flammability limits of a substance are often used as measures of its flammability hazard in a given situation.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Flammable&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Having a flash point lower than 143\u00b0 F (62\u00b0C) and greater than 100\u00b0F (38\u00b0C).<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Flash point&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; The lowest temperature to which a substance must be heated before the vapor-air mixture above it will be ignited by a free flame in the open air.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Fluorescence&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A luminescent (light-emitting) quality of an organic dye or inorganic substance. In fluorescent substances, light emission continues only as long as the excitation energy lasts. Differs from phosphorescence, in which light emission lasts for many seconds or even hours after excitation occurs. Also, in fluorescence, excitation generally is immediately followed by emission of energy, while in phosphorescence, energy emission may be delayed.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Free radical&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A molecule in which a portion is highly reactive because chemical bonds have been ruptured by thermal radiation from combustion or ionizing radiation. Conceptually, a free radical molecule contains sites with an unpaired electron available to attack other molecules. Free radicals often are involved in chain reaction-type mechanisms, such as combustion processes and the industrial processes used to make polymers.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Fuming&nbsp;&nbsp; Describes the release of fumes by highly active inorganic liquids such as nitric acid; the fumes form a noxious vapor cloud. Nitric, sulfuric, and hydrofluoric acids and similar acids produce very dangerous levels of fumes when they are in their pure state. The presence of water somewhat reduces the production of fumes.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Glacial&nbsp; &nbsp; A term used for certain acids, such as acetic or phosphoric acid, indicating a very pure form of the acid with a freezing point just below room temperature.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Hazardous chemical&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Any chemical that is a physical or health hazard <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Hazardous material&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Any substance or material in a quantity or form that may be harmful to humans, animals, crops, water systems, or other elements of the environment, if accidentally released. Hazardous materials include: explosives, gases (compressed, liquefied, or dissolved), flammable and combustible liquids, flammable solids or substances, oxidizing substances, poisonous and infectious substances, radioactive materials, and corrosives.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Heat of combustion&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; The heat generated when a substance is completely oxidized to product gases such as sulfur dioxide, carbon dioxide, and nitrogen dioxide.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Heat of crystallization&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; The heat evolved when a crystal is formed from a saturated solution of a substance.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Heat of dilution&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; The heat evolved when a solution is diluted from one concentration to a lower concentration.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Heat of hydration The heat evolved when ions in solution are hydrated. That is, the heat produced when the hydrate of a substance is formed..<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Heat of reaction&nbsp;&nbsp; The heat evolved during a chemical reaction.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Hemoglobin &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; An iron-containing protein molecule. Hemoglobin is a characteristic component of red blood cells, which carries oxygen to the tissues of the body.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Highly flammable&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Designation applying to (a) substances with flash points below 100\u00b0F, and (b) mixtures that include substances with flash points below 100\u00b0F. Materials designated as highly flammable include pyrophoric solids and substances that present an exceptional flammability hazard, in that they may suddenly and dangerously increase the intensity of a fire.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Humidity&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; The ratio of the amount of water vapor being held in the air at any given temperature to the maximum that can be held in the air at that temperature.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Hydration&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Or solvation. The association of molecules of water with inorganic substances, usually salts, to form hydrates. Also refers to the strong affinity of water molecules for ions in aqueous solution.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Hydrocarbon&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; An organic compound containing only hydrogen and carbon.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Hydrogen ion&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A hydrogen atom that has lost its single electron and consequently has a positive charge. Water (H2O) can be thought of as a combination of hydrogen ion (H+) and hydroxide ion (OH-).<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Hydrolysis&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A chemical reaction in which a bond is broken by the agency of water. A hydrogen ion and hydroxide ion from the water become independently attached to the two atoms previously linked.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Hydrolyze&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; To break down by means of reaction with water.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Hydrophilic&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Lit. \"Water-loving.\" Refers to substances that attract and retain water, and to wettable solids whose surfaces readily attract water.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Hydrophobic&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Lit. \"Water hating.\" Refers to substances that repel water and are not easily wetted or emulsified (fats, waxes, oils, metal powders, and many inorganic compounds).<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\">Hydroxide ion&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; An ion with an overall negative charge, compos</span><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 13px;\">ed of a single oxygen and a single hydrogen atom. Water (H2O) can be thought of as a combination of hydrogen ion (H+) and hydroxide ion (OH-).</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 13px;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Hygroscopic&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Capable of readily absorbing moisture from the air, so as to swell up, contract in length, or change form or consistency.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Hypergolic&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Igniting spontaneously on contact with another substance, which is typically an oxidizing agent.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">IDLH&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;  The Immediately Dangerous to Life or Health (IDLH) value represents the maximum airborne concentration of a chemical to which a healthy adult worker can be exposed and escape without suffering irreversible health effects or symptoms that impair escape (ranging from runny eyes that temporarily impair eyesight to a coma). IDLH values are derived primarily from mammalian toxicity studies.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Immediate (acute) hazard&nbsp; A hazard category that includes highly toxic, toxic, irritant, sensitizer, corrosive (as defined by 29 CFR \u00a7 1910.1200), and other hazardous chemicals that cause an adverse effect to a target organ. Such effects usually develop rapidly, result from short-term exposure, and are of short duration.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Immiscible&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Substances of the same phase (liquid or solid) that cannot be mixed in any proportion with one another..<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Impurity Usually, a very small amount of a foreign or extraneous substance that naturally or by accident exists in a substance. Many cases have been documented in which unintended impurities caused severe consequences during a chemical reaction process (often, processes such as polymerization reactions in which a small amount of impurity acted as a catalyst to initiate a runaway reaction)..<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Inert&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Non-reactive in nature. Refers to substances that have little or no chemical activity or affinity. Some of the best-known inert substances are the noble gases such as helium and neon.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Inert gas&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A vapor or gas containing sufficient oxygen to support combustion. Used to control cargo tank atmospheres and to prevent the formation of flammable mixtures.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Ingestion&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A route of chemical exposure in which a toxic material is brought into the bloodstream by entering the digestive tract.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Inhalation&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp; A route of chemical exposure in which a toxic material is brought into the bloodstream as particles or volatile compounds breathed into the lungs and nasal passages.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Inhibitor Substance that acts to retard or slow the rate of a chemical reaction. Probably the most important inhibitors are the antioxidants, which slow the oxidation of many types of materials such as rubber and food products..<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Initiator&nbsp; A substance that, because of its unusual chemical activity, may induce chemical reaction in other substances. Reactions such as polymerization, oxidation (formation of peroxides), and detonation (rapid combustion) are aided by initiators. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Inorganic&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Compounds that do not contain the element carbon, as well as the following carbon-containing compounds: the carbon oxides, the carbides, carbon disulfide, phosgene, cyanides of metals, and carbonyl sulfide.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Ion&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; An atom or group of atoms that has an overall non-zero electric charge (which may be either negative or positive).<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Irradiation&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; The impingement of radiation of a specific wavelength on a substance to initiate a chemical change.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Isomer&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Compounds sharing the same molecular weight and molecular formula, but having different chemical structures. The difference in structure often causes differences in chemical and physical properties such as boiling point, melting point, and water solubility. Property differences among isomers produce differences in their reactivity and toxicity.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Isotope&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Elements that are otherwise identical but that have different weights because they have different numbers of neutrons in their nuclei. The simplest example is the isotopes of hydrogen, including H1, normal hydrogen, and H2, or deuterium, which has an additional neutron.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Lachrymator&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Irritating to the eyes in a way that induces tears. Tear gas is a lachrymator.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Lacquer A fast-drying, organic coating material.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Lignin&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp; An amorphous organic polymer that helps bind cellulose fibers together in plant tissue.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Liquor&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp; Any one or more compound mixtures in aqueous phase.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Litmus&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp; A substance or material that, on contact with another substance, indicates that substance's pH or hydrogen ion concentration. Examples include litmus paper and pH indicator solutions. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Lower explosive limit&nbsp; (LEL)&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Or lower flammability limit. The lowest concentration of a flammable vapor in air at which explosion or combustion can occur. See also Upper Explosive Limit (UEL).<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Luminescence&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; The phenomenon in which a substance that has absorbed radiant excitation energy emits radiation on return from some excitation state to its ground state energy.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Material Safety Data Sheet&nbsp; (MSDS)&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A worksheet containing information about a hazardous chemical in the workplace. MSDSs are submitted by facility owner/operators to meet the chemical inventory reporting requirements of EPCRA. Under 29 CFR 1910.1200, facilities must develop an MSDS for each hazardous chemical present on site. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Melting point&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Also freezing point. The temperature at which the solid and liquid phases of a substance exist in equilibrium. Depends on chemical composition and applied pressure.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Mineral&nbsp; The inorganic constituents of the earth's crust. Most minerals have a definite internal structure and chemical composition.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Miscible The degree to which one substance can be mixed with another (usually, related to the degree to which a solute may mix in a particular solvent). Some materials, such as gases generally as well as ethyl alcohol in water, are completely miscible with one another in any proportion. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Mist&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Extremely small liquid particles which are suspended in a gas phase. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Mixture&nbsp; A uniform or nonuniform blend of two or more substances. Examples include blood, milk, petroleum products, and alloys.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Molar&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A concentration expressed as the number of gram molecular weights of a solute mixed into one liter of solvent, usually water. A 1-molar solution of sodium hydroxide contains 40 grams of sodium hydroxide in each liter of water.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Molecular Weight&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; The sum of the weights of all the atoms in a molecule.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Molecule&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp; A chemical entity composed of one or more elements in the form of atoms.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Monomer&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; One of the molecules that link together to make a polymer. For example, the monomer of natural rubber is isoprene. Monomers may be naturally occurring or synthetic. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Mucous membranes&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;those surfaces of the respiratory system lined with secretion like the nose , throat, windpipe and lungs.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Mutagen&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A chemical or radiation source that alters an organism's DNA, affecting transmission of inherited characteristics from one generation to the next.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">National Institute for Occupational Safety and Health (NIOSH&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Federal agency responsible for conducting research and making recommendations for the prevention of work-related disease and injury. NIOSH is part of the Centers for Disease Control and Prevention (CDC). <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">National Response Center&nbsp; (NRC)&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; The central Federal clearinghouse for information on hazardous chemical spills and other oil or hazardous substance releases.
