Responsible parties should contact the NRC in order to fulfill reporting requirements for spills of oil and hazardous substances (hotline: 1-800-424-8802) NRC is the OSRO.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">National Response Team (NRT)&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp; A planning, policy, and coordinating body consisting of representatives from 16 federal agencies with interest and expertise in aspects of emergency response to pollution incidents. The NRT provides national level policy guidance prior to an incident and can provide assistance during an incident.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Neutralization/Neutralize&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; The reaction between an acid and base to form a salt and water. Neutralization is often rapid, vigorous, and exothermic (heat-producing).<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Noble gases&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A group of six elements (helium, neon, argon, krypton, xenon, and radon) exhibiting little or no chemical reactivity. Non-combustible&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Non-reactive with air, even at very high temperatures.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Nonoxidizing&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Completely or nearly lacking the ability to oxidize (to transfer oxygen to other groups or lose electrons to other groups).<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">NOx&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;  &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The oxides of nitrogen, taken as a group. Nitrogen forms several distinct compounds with oxygen; some of these compounds convert back and forth readily under ordinary conditions.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Nucleophile&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A chemical reactant that tends to react at centers of positive charge.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Occupational Safety and Health Administration (OSHA).&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Federal agency within the U. S. Department of Labor with the responsibility of ensuring worker safety and health. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Olefin&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; An alkene. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Organic&nbsp; Generally, compounds that contain the element carbon, except for some carbon-containing compounds that are considered to be inorganic (carbon oxides, carbides, carbon disulfide, phosgene, the cyanides of the metals, and carbonyl sulfide). <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Oxidation&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp; A chemical reaction in which oxygen bonds to an element or compound. By extension, a reaction in which one element or compound rises to a higher oxidation state while another drops to a lower oxidation state (the term is used in this sense even when no oxygen whatever is present).<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Oxidation number&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; An arbitrary number assigned to an atom in a compound. Oxidation increases the total oxidation number of the atoms in a compound; reduction reduces it.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Oxidizing agent&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A material capable of bringing about oxidation (the loss of electrons) in other materials, while it is itself reduced (gains electrons). <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Peroxidizable&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Apt to react spontaneously with oxygen at room temperature, to form peroxides and other products. Most such autooxidations are accelerated by light or by trace impurities. Because many peroxides are explosive, peroxidizable compounds are especially hazardous. Ethers and aldehydes are particularly peroxidizable.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">pH&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A number indicating the acidity or alkalinity of an aqueous solution, defined as the negative logarithm of the hydrogen ion concentration in moles per liter. At room temperature, a solution having a pH of 7 is neutral (neither acidic nor basic). Solutions with pHs greater than 7 are basic (alkaline); solutions with pHs below 7 are acidic.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Pitting&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a form of corrosion as little holes on the steel surface. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Polymer The product of polymerization. Proteins, starches, cellulose and natural rubber are naturally occurring polymers; polystyrene, nylon, Teflon, and synthetic rubber are synthetic polymers. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Polymerizable&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Capable of undergoing polymerization, an energy-releasing self-reaction. The products of polymerization reactions are generally less reactive than the starting materials. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Polymerization&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A chemical reaction in which a large number of smaller molecules (monomer units) join together by chemically linking into chains or networks (polymers). Energy is released during polymerization reactions<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">ppb&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Parts per billion. Units used to express the concentration of a gas or vapor in air (as molecules of chemical per billion molecules of air).<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">ppm&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Parts per million. Units used to express the concentration of a gas or vapor in air (as molecules of chemical per million molecules of air).<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Prill&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Small spherical or cylindrical pellets used in the fertilizer and explosive industry, because they are convenient to handle. An example is ammonium nitrate prills, which are often coated with a wax because this salt has a tendency to cake when hydrated.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Pyrophoric&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Any substance that ignites in the presence of air at or below ambient temperatures. Many pyrophoric materials react with moisture in the air to generate flammable hydrogen gas and enough heat to ignite the hydrogen. These are extremely dangerous fire hazards that are generally stored under an inert atmosphere or in a solvent like ether or kerosene that excludes air.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Pyrotechnics&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; The manufacture of fireworks, signal flares, and so on, involving the mixture of different chemicals to achieve various visual and auditory effects. Chemicals used in pyrotechnics include many explosive inorganic compounds such as potassium nitrate, metal perchlorates, dichromate, powdered metals, and phosphorus.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Radiation&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp; Electromagnetic energy or light, depending on the wavelength, which imparts energy to molecules and atoms. Radiation absorption causes ionization and bond-breaking.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Radical&nbsp;&nbsp; In inorganic chemistry, refers to an aqueous, dissociated ionized group. In organic chemistry, refers to an uncharged alkyl, aryl, or other group that acts as a fragmented, highly reactive, short-lived substance. Free radical generation is a very important reaction that can initiate polymerization and other kinds of reactions.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Rapid reaction&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;A reaction in which chemical change becomes evident within minutes to hours after the mixing of incompatible chemicals. That evidence can be dramatic change such as fire or explosion, or more subtle effects, such as chemical heat production, evolution of gases, or deposition/disappearance of solids.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Rare&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Can refer either to the noble gases (helium, neon, and argon), the rare-earth elements (or lanthanide series, starting with lantanum), or rare metals such as gold, silver, cadmium, and platinum.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Reactive A hazard category that includes chemicals described as unstable, reactive, organic peroxide, or water-reactive <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Reactive group&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Reactive groups are categories of chemicals that react in similar ways because they are similar in their chemical structure. For purposes of predicting reactivity between mixed chemicals, each substance in the Chemical Library has been assigned to one or more reactive groups, based on the known chemistry of that substance<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Reactive hazard&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Some chemicals pose special or acute reactivity-related hazards that are intrinsic to those chemicals because of their structures and known physical characteristics. special reactive hazards include a chemical's tendency to be flammable, explosive (either by itself or when mixed with other materials), peroxidizable, polymerizable, air- and or water- reactive, radioactive, or a strong oxidizer or reducer.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Reactivity&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; The tendency of a substance to take part in chemical change. The reactivity of most kinds of substances depends on the temperature and pressure of the surroundings, and on the identity and physical form of other chemicals with which a given substance is in contact. In contrast, innately reactive substances include those that react rapidly with water, air, and other common components of the environment under ordinary conditions, as well as substances that self-react (decompose or polymerize) under ordinary conditions.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Reagent Any chemical substance used in chemical analysis.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Redox&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A contraction for \"oxidation-reduction.\" Redox reactions, in which electrons are transferred from a reducing agent to an oxidizing agent, are a major category of chemical change.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Reducing agent&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A substance that can bring about reduction (gaining of electrons) in other substances, while it is itself oxidized (loses electrons). <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Reduction&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A reaction in which either oxygen is removed from a substance or, in a more general sense, one or more electrons is accepted from another substance. (Can also mean a process in metallurgy by which materials are separated into their wanted and unwanted components from an ore body.) Contrast with Oxidation.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Resins&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Naturally-occurring \"essential oils\" that are water-insoluble and extracted from natural sources, such as trees and shrubs. Also, synthetic polymers such as polystyrene or polyethylene, even though such materials are not complex mixtures of compounds like other resins, but instead are long, complex polymers.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Risk analysis&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A systematic method of assessing the damage that could be caused to a community by a hazardous substance release.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Salt&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; An ionic compound derived from the combination of cations (positively-charged ions) with anions (negatively-charged ions). Sodium chloride (common table salt) is an example.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Saturated&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp; Refers to organic compounds that contain the maximum possible number of hydrogen atoms per carbon atom. Also used to describe a solution of a solute that is at its solubility limit in a given solvent system at a specified temperature.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Skin absorption&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Chemical exposure through the skin. Because the skin does not act as a reliable barrier to hazardous chemicals, it can be a route of acute poisoning. Compounds such as dimethyl sulfoxide are known to be directly absorbed into the bloodstream through the skin.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Sludge&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp; A thick or viscous mixture of solids in aqueous solution, such as sewage sludge.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Slurry&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A dilute mixture or suspension of solid particles in water, such as clay, fiber, or metal powders.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Soda ash&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Sodium carbonate.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Solute/Solvent&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A solute is a gas, liquid, or solid substance that is uniformly dispersed in a liquid solvent substance, forming a solution. The solvent molecules act to break the solute molecules' attraction for one another, and also the solvent's natural structure. For instance, water is a highly-structured substance, in the absence of any solutes. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Solution A molecularly uniform mixture of one or more solutes in a solvent. Sometimes, one or more of the solutes are ionized in solution. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Specific gravity&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; The ratio of the density of a substance at a given temperature to the density of water at the same temperature. A substance with a specific gravity greater than 1.0 will sink rather than float in water.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Spectroscopy&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; The qualitative and quantitative analysis of emitted and absorbed energy, done by subjecting a substance to electromagnetic energy. The wavelength of this excitation energy can vary from gamma and x-ray to radio frequency.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Stabilizer&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;  Any substance that, when added to another, acts to prevent or retard chemical or physical change in the latter. Examples include antioxidants, inhibitors, and emulsifying agents.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Starch&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A carbohydrate or polysaccharide polymer composed of amylose and amylpectin. Starch occurs in plant tissues such as potatoes, tapioca, and rice, and is used as a thickening agent in foods.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Static accumulator&nbsp;&nbsp; A liquid with an electrical continuity of less than 50 pico Siemens / metre , so that it is capable of retaining a significant electrostatic charge.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Strong oxidizing agent&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Oxidizing agents gain electrons from other substances and are themselves thereby chemically reduced. Strong oxidizing agents accept electrons particularly readily from many other substances. The ensuing redox reactions may be vigorous or violent and may release new substances that may take part in further additional reactions. Keep strong oxidizing agents well separated from strong reducing agents.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Strong reducing agent&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Reducing agents give up electrons to other substances, and are themselves thereby oxidized. Strong reducing agents donate electrons particularly readily to many other substances. The ensuing redox reactions may be vigorous or violent and may generate new substances that take part in further additional reactions. Keep strong reducing agents well away from strong oxidizing agents.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Sublime&nbsp; The change of a substance from the solid state to the vapor state, without passing through the liquid intermediate state. Substances that sublime include solid carbon dioxide, sulfur, camphor, and naphthalene.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Surfactant&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A substance that reduces surface tension of liquids. Nearly synonymous with detergent (which reduces the surface tension of water), wetting agent, and emulsifier.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Suspension&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A uniformly-dispersed mixture of fine particles in a liquid.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Synonyms&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A single chemical may have many names. The synonyms by which a chemical is named can include common names in different languages, trade names, and other names.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Technical grade&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Term applied to substances that are unrefined, impure, and/or less than 100% pure grade.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Thermoplastic&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Any substance that is solid or semisolid at room temperature, but becomes liquid when heated. Thermoplastic substances can be molded or shaped and hold their shape until heated. Examples include butter, waxes, and certain polymers.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Threat zone&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A threat zone encloses the area around the location of a hazardous chemical release, within which concentrations of the chemical could reach or exceed a specified LOC (level of concern). <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">TLV &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;threshold limit value. Allowed exposure dose. STEL: short term exposure limit. TWA: time weighted average (longer period exposure limit).<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">UN/NA number&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Or UN number. A chemical identification number, assigned under a numbering system developed by the U.S. Department of Transportation. This system has since become the United Nations standard system for classifying hazardous materials.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Unsaturated&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Refers to organic compounds that contain fewer than the maximum possible number of hydrogen atoms per carbon atom. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Upper Explosive Limit (UEL)&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; The highest concentration of a flammable vapor in air at which explosion or combustion can occur. Above this concentration, the vapor-air mixture is too rich to combust. See also Lower explosive limit (LEL).<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">UV&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Abbreviation for Ultraviolet radiation.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Vapor density&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; The ratio of the density of a gas to the density of air at the same temperature. A gas with a vapor density greater than 1.0 is heavier than air and will sink in the atmosphere. <o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Vapor pressure&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; In a closed system containing an evaporating liquid and its vapor, the equilibrium at which the number of vapor molecules reentering the liquid equals the number going from the liquid to the vapor phase. Vapor pressure is commonly expressed in pressure units of either millimeters of mercury (mm Hg), pounds per square inch (psi), or atmospheres (atm).<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Viscosity The tendency of a liquid substance to resist movement or flow due to an external force applied to it.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Volatile/Volatility&nbsp; Refers to the ease with which a substance goes from liquid or solid phase to the vapor phase (via evaporation or sublimation). The volatility of a given substance increases with temperature.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Water of crystallization&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Water chemically combined within a crystalline substance.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Water-reactive&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Substances that may react rapidly or violently with liquid water and steam, typically forming toxic and/or flammable products and heat.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Water solubility&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Mixing of gas, liquid, or solid materials in water. The highest amount of a particular material that can be mixed in water is its water solubility. Water solubility ranges shown in Chemical Library records are as follows: Water insoluble: &lt;1 mg/ml; Slightly water soluble: 1-10mg/ml; Water soluble: &gt;10 mg/ml.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">Wettable powder&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A solid material whose surface is hydrophilic, and therefore attracts water.<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"font-size: 11pt; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Calibri, sans-serif; font-size: 10pt;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\"><o:p></o:p></span></span></div><br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"></div><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"></div><div class=\"WordSection1\">  <div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue; font-family: 'Times New Roman', serif;\"><b><br />\n</b></span></div></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: blue;\">CAPT&nbsp;
